Introduction
The Islamic world at the end of the third century was the Muhammadan Hijrah
With the character of science, philosophy and literature, it controls his cultural circle and his society
Al-Alami New Calls, Complex Doctrinal Differences, and the Controversy of My Words Was Not
It ends at someone or stands in a certain place. And how useful is it for the researcher who
He wants to study the origin of these differences in depth and try to see the opinions of
Writers and scholars who lived in that distant era, and left scientific traces
And new ways of expressing their time and understanding of philosophical issues and the extent of
Their diligence in the interpretation of texts and the interpretation of verses, then they can be
A reasonable opinion that can be used to bring reality and truth.
The aforementioned disputes were often out of scope
The oral discussions that used to be raised in the clubs and scientific centers are developing
To long lectures that appear on the pages of books and publications. And from the difference
which contributed a large share in this field ((Ismailia)) but it is strange

by converting the doctrine of the Samanid state in Azerbaijan to Ismailism, and he was executed
The year - 331 AH (and 942 AD) - as stated in the book (The Difference Between the Differences)) by its author
Abdul Qadir al-Baghdadi, and it is very strange that (the argument of the Iraqis) is its bidder.

Among Ismaili intellectuals and scholars at that time, Abu Hatim was motivated

Al-Razi:
He is Abu Hatem Ahmed bin Hamdan Al-Lifi Al-Warsnani Al-Razi and his name is Ismailia
Our master (Abu Hatim) exaggerated. He was a preacher of Ismailism in the land of irrigation and then
He moved to Baghdad, where he took it as his residence. He doesn't know his date of birth
Exactly. The activity of the Ismaili da'wah during the reign of the Imamate of Muhammad al-Mahdi Balsha (1)
(Ubayd Allah) is the founder of the Fatimid state in Morocco. He was distinguished by the sweetness of his speech
And his good eloquence, which is famous for him, attracted him (Al-Marwazi), the prince of irrigation and he was
Sunni extremist and has been persuading the princes of those countries to enter Ismailia
Until he became one of the flags of politics and religion and one of the guides of the Islamic scientific renaissance
In the late third and early fourth centuries, he was taking refuge in the
Theological and philosophical sciences. The great orientalist Paul Krauss (2) said about him:
He was a leading preacher of Ismailia and played an important role in political affairs
In Tabaristan and Daylam, especially in Rai and Isfahan, until the elders responded to him
Statesmen such as Asfar bin Shirawayh, Mardawikh Al-Qa'id, and others. And the truth
Abu Hatem Al-Razi was one of the flags of the scientific renaissance not in Ismailia
Not only in the Islamic world, but in the Islamic world, and he contributed to the dissemination of philosophical teachings in all
Eastern countries, especially in the periphery of the general Islamic culture, and despite all the
(1) This Imam lived in Samia, Syria, and migrated from there to Morocco when the pressure of the Abbasids intensified.

He was not spared from the persecution of the enemies in Daylam, and he was forced to disappear.
In the last years of his life, he died in 322 AH after the Fatimid Qa'im took over the affairs of the
The Ismaili Imamate in the Maghreb, and he was sixty-two years old, as he said
Some historians.
He was a contemporary of Abu Bakr Muhammad bin Zakaria Al-Razi, the famous physician and author of
Well-known philosophical views in which he came out on many of Aristotle's theories
naturalistic and metaphysical denying the reconciliation of philosophy and religion, believing that
Philosophy is the only way to reform the individual and society. And it went between them, i.e.
Violent and multiple discussions between the Razis, which were attended by some scholars and presidents
Politicians, and Abu Hatim recorded these discussions in his book (Flags of the Prophethood)
If he does not name the person to whom he is criticizing, he calls him an atheist.
There is conclusive evidence that this atheist was none other than Razi Abu Bakr.
The great philosopher Al-Kirmani (Hajjat al-Iraqin) has mentioned in his book
(The Golden Sayings) that discussions about prophecy and legal rituals took place between
Abu Bakr Al-Razi and Abu Hatim in Al-Rai Island during the days of Mardawikh and in his presence and in his presence
Abu Hatim was able to degrade Abu Bakr al-Razi and renounce his views in his book (Flags)
Prophethood) with pages overflowing with charm and miracles, in which he has closed the eyes of those who are arrogant.
And those who are stubborn are the means of getting rid of and fleeing.
His most important works are the book ((Al-Zeina)) (1) in Arabic letters, their derivatives and reasons
Its situation and the meanings of the words, and it is a great book in the authentic Arabic cams
And the extruder in which the Qur'an was pronounced and enacted by the Muslims and from which it became
Islamic terminology, and the number of pages of this book is 1200 pages.
He dedicated it to the Fatimid Imam who succeeded Muhammad al-Mahdi Billah ( Ubaidullah ) and to him

Al-Sijistani:
The book "Flags of Prophethood", "Al-Islah", "Al-Jami'" and others.
Abu Ya'qub Ishaq al-Sijistani or (al-Sijzi) is considered to be at the forefront of scholars.
who have struggled, worked and dedicated themselves to establishing cosmic philosophical rules
On ideological intellectual foundations and solid scientific foundations and fixed pillars no
It trembles no matter what crises happen to it. In fact, he is one of those who sacrificed
with all they have in order to spread it and circulate it in other countries even
Late in his life, he was accused of blasphemy and atheism by the conservative public and was finally killed
For the sake of his faith. Al-Sijistani played an important role in the field of philosophy and led
The postponement of intellectual services in the third century of the Hijrah and its intellectual impact appeared
In his pupil Hamid al-Din al-Kirmani (Hajjat al-Iraqiyyen) who followed his curriculum
He called for his teachings and the rise of the flood of his springs. And if we know that Al-Kirmani
Philosophy lesson in Al-Sijistani school of thought we could put Al-Sijistani in
The first rank among the famous Muslim scholars, thinkers and philosophers of the world.
He was a contemporary of the esoteric Ismaili call in the Age of Revelation, i.e., a period of prosperity.

In these lines, we summarize the views of al-Sijistani on theology as expressed in
Most of his writings, he believes that the creator of female creators is an ancient, high and ancient creator in
Finding the primacy, and that the world of beings and creators is up-to-date because if it is not
It must have been something that preceded it, even if the world was old.
Before the Creator because it is impossible to attach His might to the old and His existence to nothingness and to necessity
He is the one who is transcendent of the realization of the attributes, so that he does not attain by sense and does not fall
Under the eyes and the eyes do not perceive him and he is not called naturalized and does not think of suspicion or
The eyes see it, and it is not described by the senses, nor is it perceived by analogy, nor is it like people, for it is
Al-Manzah against Manaf or Nad Mukaf or something like that, exalt him from the semi-limited
The illusions in the description of his might were confused and the understanding of the character of his kingdom was shortened.
Seeing without realizing His greatness, He has no likeness or likeness, and he is not equal and unlike.
This is against because the opposite is against it is an opponent that indicates his identity by his creation and its effects on
His names are like his prophets, the mind has no room or analogy in attaining his heavens, as an analogy
The creative with his creator is impossible, he is the reason for everything that exists because he is the creator of the creative women and an inventor
The inventors and the reason for beings and the Lord of all things and the creator and complement and informant
To the best of circumstances. He is bounded by a thought or surrounded by an appreciation that he does not have.
Names because the names were put for his existences and not attributes because the attributes are from his essences;
And that the letters of the language cannot lead to the pronunciation of his name or to be called
Some of them because they are all of his inventions and that all the names he created made him
He is an ancient and pre-eternal source and the owner of the source of primacy in order.
Because the first limit emerged from it and the first one overflowed from it while it is creative
The creators, the ill explainer, the barry of the praya, and the perpetual who exists in his individuality and steadfastness.
The first act of creation was accompanied by the first number, which made it the origin of the numbers, as
The intellect has made it the origin of the creatures and the original speaker of the world of religion, and it is added
In addition to all this, it does not acquire any of the attributes, and that it is not a body, nor is it in

<!-- page 253 -->
comparée entre celle-ci et les théories philosophiques officielles des
ismaïlites.
Si la série d'ouvrages historiques et philosophiques déjà éta-
blis et publies par nos soins s'enrichit aujourd'hui d'un volume
nouveau, «ar-riad», cela ne saurait se faire sans un mot de recon-
naissant hommage à l'eminent orientaliste qu'est Professeur W.
Ivanow. Car c'est grâce à son infatigable initiative au service de
la science que la plupart des manuscrits ismaéliens ont pu être
mis à jour. Travail enorme et desintéressé qu'inspire un seul sou-
ci: celui d'informer le monde islamique sur cette philosophie uni-
verselle qui fit bouillonner les esprits pour un temps, fascina le
regard des savants et fut, en Orient comme en Occident, à la fine
pointe de leurs approximations.
Beyrouth - Liban
1960
-251-
Aref Tamer

<!-- page 254 -->
le profit pour qui recherche l'origine de ces controverses, lorsqu'il
s'applique à creuser les diverses opinions. Il découvre que l'œuvre
des auteurs de cette époque lointaine constitue un monument de
science nouvelle par rapport à leur siècle, tant pour la penetra-
tion des problèmes philosophiques que pour l'ampleur de la re-
cherche dans le domaine des commentaires de textes et de l'exé-
gèse des versets coraniques. Cet effort leur a valu d'approcher
de la réalité et de s'en faire une conception raisonnée.
La plupart du temps les controverses en question avaient
pour origine des discussions orales que se livraient les cercles et
les centres d'études scientifiques. Elles prenaient la forme de lon-
gues conférences qui s'étalent dans les livres à longueur de pages.
Parmi les groupements qui contribuaient abondamment à ces dé-
bats, nous trouvons celui des Ismaéliens. Mais ce qui est assez
surprenant, c'est que, ces débats de théologie à peine terminés
entre différentes sectes, nous voyons les Ismaéliens s'engager
dans un autre genre de controverse, un genre tout nouveau ... C'est
la controverses entre leurs Da'is eux-mêmes. Ceci prouve claire-
ment que la liberté de pensée était chez eux une loi souveraine.
Le dynamisme de leur réflexion intellectuelle, affranchie des chaî-
nes de la tradition, s'imposait ainsi aux milieu conservateurs et
les forçait à l'abandon des positions surannées.
L'ouvrage intitulé «al-mahsul> parut dans les milieux ismaé-
liens au début du 4ème siècle de l'Hégire (10ème siècle après Jésus-
Christ). Il est attribué au Da'i an-Nasafi, il est curieux qu'al-
Kirmani, en parlant de ce texte, omette de mentionner son auteur.
Peut-être cette omission est-elle un indice que le livre a été attri-
bue par erreur a an-Nasafi. La faveur obtenue par «al-mahsul>
dans les milieux ismaéliens amena le Da'i Abu Hatim ar-Razi à
rédiger de son côté un écrit intitulé «al-islah>. Ce livre renferme
une critique de certaines opinions rapportées par «al-mahsul».
Cette discussion poussa un autre grand Da'i, Abu Ya'qub as-Sijis-
tani, à intervenir à son tour contre ce qu'il estimait contraire à la
vérité et aux principes philosophiques. Dans son livre «an-nasra»
il prit le parti de l'auteur d'«al-mahsul» et critiqua ar-Razi sans
toutefois chercher à ruiner la position de celui-ci.
Peu de temps après lui, al-Kirmani aborda le même sujet de
façon magistrale. Ce fut dans ce précieux traité «ar-riad»: il se
donna le rôle d'arbitre entre les auteurs d'«al-islah> et d'«an-nas-
ra» et sut, avec une habileté consommée, à la fois combler d'éloges
et critiquer avec rigueur scientifique les différentes positions des
trois livres, en les confrontant avec la doctrine fondamentale de
l'Ismaélisme. Autrement dit, son ouvrage constitue une étude
-252-

<!-- page 255 -->
Le livre que nous présentons aujourd'hui aux experts de
sciences philosophiques s'appelle «ar-riad». Il a pour auteur
Sayyidna Hamid ad-Din Ahmad b. Abdallah al-Kirmani qui était
Da'i de l'Imam fatimite, le khalife, Al-Hakim bi-Amrillah en Irag
et en Perse. Il portait le surnom de «Hujjat al-'Iragain» (charge
de la mission ismaélienne pour ces deux régions).
-
Les chefs religieux ismaeliens comptent «ar-riad> au nombre
des ouvrages importants s'adressant aux plus instruits de ceux
qui occupent les premiers rangs de la secte. Il se caractérise de ce
fait par le niveau élevé et la force de sa doctrine. Cela explique
que les débutants en matière de recherche philosophique aient
éprouvé de la difficulté à comprendre les implications de ce texte,
à pénétrer les nuances de son vocabulaire technique.
«Ar-riad» marque une étape dans l'évolution de la pensée is-
lamique et nous présente une image claire de la croissance de l'édi-
fice doctrinal ismaélien. Et quand nous savons que le livre expose
en raccourci l'enseignement prépondérant de cette période de
l'Ismaélisme, nous comprenons quelle influence il a pu exercer. Il
est de bonnes raisons pour considérer ce texte comme une confé-
rence générale de philosophie qu'élaborèrent quatre des grands
Da'is ismaéliens de la première période, en y insérant leurs efforts
de réflexion philosophique ainsi que leur exégèse ésotérique. Ce
sont: le Da'i Muhammad b. Ahmad an-Nasafi, Abu Hatim ar-Razi,
Abu Ya'qub as-Sijistani et Hamid ad-Din al-Kirmani. Dans cette
œuvre commune de critique les quatre penseurs s'adonnèrent pas-
sionnément à la défense de leur spéculation et y condensèrent leur
doctrine.
4
Il est aujourd'hui admis que vers la fin du 3ème siècle de
l'Hegir le monde islamique offrait les traits dun état de culture -
scientifique, philosophique et littéraire - avancé, mais travaillé
par des messages nouveaux et des controverses doctrinales va-
riées. Les théologiens se livraient alors à des débats sans fin, dé-
gages de tout fixisme dans l'expression. Quel n'est pas dès lors
-253-
